# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

I've completed a comprehensive analysis of prototype pollution defense mechanisms in Node.js core JavaScript modules. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I discovered **92 JavaScript source files** in `nodejs/node` that implement prototype pollution defenses using multiple complementary strategies:

### Key Defense Patterns:

1. **Primordials System** (`lib/internal/per_context/primordials.js`): Safe wrappers for built-in objects with frozen, null-prototype implementations (SafeMap, SafeSet, SafeWeakMap, SafePromise variants, etc.)

2. **Null-Prototype Objects** (`{ __proto__: null }`): Used across 30+ files for safe property storage in HTTP agents, configuration objects, and utility modules

3. **ObjectPrototypeHasOwnProperty Checks**: Defensive property validation in buffer, cluster, crypto, and validation modules to prevent inherited property lookups

4. **ObjectCreate(null)**: Creates objects without prototype chains for safe configuration and error serialization

5. **ObjectSetPrototypeOf Hardening**: Explicit prototype chain control in network, stream, and worker modules

6. **ESLint Enforcement**: `tools/eslint-rules/avoid-prototype-pollution.js` enforces patterns and flags unsafe built-in method calls

### Coverage:

The defenses are consistently applied across all major core modules including:
- HTTP modules (_http_agent.js, _http_server.js, _http_client.js)
- Network modules (net.js, dgram.js, tls)
- Stream modules (transform, duplex, passthrough)
- Worker/cluster modules
- File system modules
- Test runner and performance monitoring
- Crypto and WebIDL modules

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, key symbols, and a detailed narrative explanation.

strategies:\\n\\n## 1. Primordials-Based Protection (lib/internal/per_context/primordials.js)\\n\\nThe cornerstone of Node's defense is the primordials system, which creates safe, frozen wrappers of built-in objects to prevent prototype pollution attacks. Key components include:\\n\\n- **makeSafe()** function: Creates safe subclasses of built-in constructors (Map, Set, WeakMap, WeakSet, Promise, etc.) by freezing their prototypes and setting them to null via ObjectSetPrototypeOf(safe.prototype, null)\\n- **Safe* Classes**: SafeMap, SafeSet, SafeWeakMap, SafeWeakSet, SafeArrayIterator, and Safe Promise variants that replace their unsafe counterparts throughout the codebase\\n- **Object Definition**: Uses ReflectDefineProperty with `{ __proto__: null, ...desc }` pattern to safely define properties, preventing prototype chain attacks\\n\\n## 2. Null-Prototype Object Pattern\\n\\nNumerous core modules use `{ __proto__: null }` object literals for safe property storage:\\n- lib/v8.js, lib/vm.js, lib/quic.js: Use null-prototype objects for constants and configuration\\n- lib/_http_agent.js, lib/_http_outgoing.js: Safely store HTTP options with `{ __proto__: null, ...options }`\\n- lib/internal/webidl.js, lib/internal/options.js: Safe dictionary creation with null prototypes\\n- lib/internal/util/inspect.js, lib/internal/heap_utils.js, lib/internal/event_target.js: Property definitions with null prototypes\\n\\n## 3. ObjectPrototypeHasOwnProperty Pattern\\n\\nCore modules defensively use ObjectPrototypeHasOwnProperty for safe property checks:\\n- lib/buffer.js, lib/cluster.js, lib/internal/tty.js: Check own properties to avoid inherited prototype properties\\n- lib/child_process.js, lib/internal/errors.js: Validate object properties without triggering prototype lookups\\n- lib/internal/util/inspect.js, lib/internal/validators.js: Safe property iteration and checking\\n- lib/internal/crypto/util.js, lib/internal/crypto/webidl.js: Secure algorithm/parameter validation\\n\\n## 4. ObjectCreate(null) with Safe Properties\\n\\nFiles that create null-prototype objects with protected properties:\\n- lib/quic.js: Uses ObjectCreate(null, { __proto__: null, ...properties })\\n- lib/internal/error_serdes.js: Creates `const all = { __proto__: null }` for error property serialization\\n- lib/internal/console/global.js: ReflectDefineProperty with null-prototype descriptors\\n- lib/internal/worker/io.js: Safely creates property descriptors with null prototypes\\n\\n## 5. Prototype Chain Hardening with ObjectSetPrototypeOf\\n\\nCore modules set safe prototypes explicitly:\\n- lib/net.js, lib/dgram.js: `ObjectSetPrototypeOf(Server.prototype, EventEmitter.prototype)`\\n- lib/buffer.js: `ObjectSetPrototypeOf(Buffer, Uint8Array)`\\n- lib/internal/per_context/domexception.js: `ObjectSetPrototypeOf(safe.prototype, null)`\\n- lib/internal/freeze_intrinsics.js: Deep freezing of intrinsic objects to prevent prototype pollution\\n\\n## 6. ESLint Enforcement\\n\\ntools/eslint-rules/avoid-prototype-pollution.js enforces:\\n- Null-prototype objects for property descriptors\\n- Safe primordial usage patterns\\n- Avoidance of unsafe built-in methods that lookup prototype properties\\n- Proxy handler null-prototype requirement\\n\\n## 7. ObjectCreate(null) with Safe Properties\\n\\nFiles that create null-prototype objects with protected properties:\\n- lib/quic.js: Uses ObjectCreate(null, { __proto__: null, ...properties })\\n- lib/internal/error_serdes.js: Creates `const all = { __proto__: null }` for error property serialization\\n- lib/internal/console/global.js: ReflectDefineProperty with null-prototype descriptors\\n- lib/internal/worker/io.js: Safely creates property descriptors with null prototypes\\n\\n## 5. Prototype Chain Hardening with ObjectSetPrototypeOf\\n\\nCore modules set safe prototypes explicitly:\\n- lib/net.js, lib/dgram.js: `ObjectSetPrototypeOf(Server.prototype, EventEmitter.prototype)`\\n- lib/buffer.js: `ObjectSetPrototypeOf(Buffer, Uint8Array)`\\n- lib/internal/per_context/domexception.js: `ObjectSetPrototypeOf(safe.prototype, null)`\\n- lib/internal/freeze_intrinsics.js: Deep freezing of intrinsic objects to prevent prototype pollution\\n\\n## 6. ESLint Enforcement\\n\\ntools/eslint-rules/avoid-prototype-pollution.js enforces:\\n- Null-prototype objects for property descriptors\\n- Safe primordial usage patterns\\n- Avoidance of unsafe built-in methods that lookup prototype properties\\n- Proxy handler null-prototype requirement\\n\\n## 7. High-Level Module Protection\\n\\nCluster, worker, test runner, and stream modules universally use Safe* versions:\\n- lib/internal/cluster/: Uses SafeMap, SafeSet for handle and worker tracking\\n- lib/internal/test_runner/: SafeMap for test assertions, SafeSet for tracking\\n- lib/internal/streams/: ObjectSetPrototypeOf patterns for stream hierarchy\\n- lib/internal/perf/: SafeMap for performance metrics and user timing\\n\\nThis multi-layered approach ensures that user-controlled input cannot pollute the prototype chain of critical system objects, protecting against both direct and indirect prototype pollution attacks throughout Node.js core.\"\n}\n",
